					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
<h2 id="victims">Victims</h2>
<p>Based on our visibility we know that ToddyCat focused its attention on high-profile targets; most of them were government organizations and military entities, as well as military contractors.</p>
<p>We know the attacks launched before February 2021 targeted a very limited number of government entities in:</p>
<ul>
<li>Taiwan</li>
<li>Vietnam</li>
</ul>
<p>After the ProxyLogon publication the number of detections rapidly increased around the world, and we also observed victims in the following countries:</p>
<ul>
<li>Afghanistan</li>
<li>India</li>
<li>Iran</li>
<li>Malaysia</li>
<li>Pakistan</li>
<li>Russia</li>
<li>Slovakia</li>
<li>Thailand</li>
<li>United Kingdom</li>
</ul>
<p>After May 2021, we observed other variants and campaigns that we attributed to the same group and affected most of the previously mentioned countries in Asia and the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Kyrgyzstan</li>
<li>Uzbekistan</li>
<li>Indonesia</li>
</ul>
<p style="text-align: center"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2022/06/21075720/APT_ToddyCat_map.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2022/06/21075720/APT_ToddyCat_map-1024x576.png" alt="ToddyCat victims map" width="1024" height="576" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-106818" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2022/06/21075720/APT_ToddyCat_map-1024x576.png 1024w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2022/06/21075720/APT_ToddyCat_map-300x169.png 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2022/06/21075720/APT_ToddyCat_map-768x432.png 768w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2022/06/21075720/APT_ToddyCat_map-1536x864.png 1536w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2022/06/21075720/APT_ToddyCat_map-800x450.png 800w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2022/06/21075720/APT_ToddyCat_map-311x175.png 311w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2022/06/21075720/APT_ToddyCat_map-370x208.png 370w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2022/06/21075720/APT_ToddyCat_map-498x280.png 498w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2022/06/21075720/APT_ToddyCat_map.png 1920w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px" /></a><br />
<strong><em>Overall affected victims map</em></strong></p>
<h2 id="attribution">Attribution</h2>
<p>Unfortunately, we were not able to attribute the attacks to a known APT group; and for this reason we dubbed this entity ToddyCat.</p>
<p>During our investigations we noticed that ToddyCat victims are related to countries and sectors usually targeted by multiple Chinese-speaking groups. In fact, we observed three different high-profile organizations compromised during a similar time frame by ToddyCat and another Chinese-speaking APT group that used the FunnyDream backdoor.</p>
<p>This overlap caught our attention, since the ToddyCat malware cluster is rarely seen as per our telemetry; and we observed the same targets compromised by both APTs in three different countries. Moreover, in all the cases there was a proximity in the staging locations and in one case they used the same directory.</p>
<p><strong>Target 1</strong><br />
C:\ProgramData\Microsoft\DRM\rundll.dll – FunnyDream related<br />
C:\ProgramData\Microsoft\mf\svchost.dll – ToddyCat</p>
<p><strong>Target 2</strong><br />
C:\ProgramData\adobe\avps.exe – FunnyDream related<br />
C:\ProgramData\adobe\2.dll – ToddyCat</p>
<p>Despite the overlap, we do not feel confident merging ToddyCat with the FunnyDream cluster at the moment. Considering the high-profile nature of all the victims we discovered, it is likely they were of interest to several APT groups. Moreover, despite the occasional proximity in staging locations, we have no concrete evidence of the two malware families directly interacting (for instance, one deploying the other), and the specific directories are frequently used by multiple attackers.</p>
<h2 id="conclusions">Conclusions</h2>
<p>ToddyCat is a sophisticated APT group that uses multiple techniques to avoid detection and thereby keeps a low profile. During our investigations we discovered dozens of samples, but despite the number of files and the duration of their activities, we were unable to attribute the attacks to a known group; and there is also quite a bit of technical information about the operations that we don&#8217;t have.</p>
<p>The affected organizations, both governmental and military, show that this group is focused on very high-profile targets and is probably used to achieve critical goals, likely related to geopolitical interests.</p>
<p>Based on our telemetry, the group shows a strong interest in targets in Southeast Asia, but their activities also impact targets in the rest of Asia and Europe.</p>
<p>We&#8217;ll continue to monitor this group and keep you updated.</p>
<p>More information, IoCs and YARA rules about ToddyCat are available to customers of the Kaspersky Intelligence Reporting Service. Contact: <a href="mailto:intelreports@kaspersky.com">intelreports@kaspersky.com</a>.</p>
